  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2e4a381b-3459-42d8-8288-2d6cf205bbe6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer6026367284429054964">As a world-ending war surges to life around them, Todd and Viola face monstrous decisions. The indigenous Spackle, thinking and acting as one, have mobilized to avenge their murdered people. Ruthless human leaders prepare to defend their factions at all costs, even as a convoy of new settlers approaches. And as the ceaseless Noise lays all thoughts bare, the projected will</span>
  <span id="freeText6026367284429054964" style="display:none">As a world-ending war surges to life around them, Todd and Viola face monstrous decisions. The indigenous Spackle, thinking and acting as one, have mobilized to avenge their murdered people. Ruthless human leaders prepare to defend their factions at all costs, even as a convoy of new settlers approaches. And as the ceaseless Noise lays all thoughts bare, the projected will of the few threatens to overwhelm the desperate desire of the many. The consequences of each action, each word, are unspeakably vast: To follow a tyrant or a terrorist? To save the life of the one you love most or thousands of strangers? To believe in redemption or assume it is lost? Becoming adults amid the turmoil, Todd and Viola question all they have known, racing through horror and outrage toward a shocking finale.</span>

<a href="/questions/1698332-what-i-don-t-understand-is-how-lee-can"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What I don't understand is how Lee can "see" through Wilf's noise. What it sounds like is being described are the pictures that go along with noise, kind of like the way the Spackle communicate. But if he's blind, he shouldn't be able to see those pictures. Does it just mean he can hear Wilf's noise? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/22082596-carlos">Carlos</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Can you imagine pictures? Can you do so with your eyes closed? Visualisation in your mind is only related to your eyes in so far as you use the things<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Can you imagine pictures? Can you do so with your eyes closed? Visualisation in your mind is only related to your eyes in so far as you use the things you have seen to visualise what you are imagining. Being blind would not affect this<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1347124-the-whole-series-seems-to-be-set-along-the">The whole series seems to be set along the length of the river valley. Can anyone tell me if there is any mention of anyone ever leaving the valley, or a reason why they haven&#39;t?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1347124'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F20758105-monsters-of-men">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1347124-the-whole-series-seems-to-be-set-along-the">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1347124-the-whole-series-seems-to-be-set-along-the">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/62795006-sydney-stene"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1508014527i/62795006._UY100_CR25,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/62795006-sydney-stene">Sydney Stene</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Nobody leaves in the main series, but in a short story Ness wrote placed shortly after the events of Monsters of Men, a small expedition is sent out t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Nobody leaves in the main series, but in a short story Ness wrote placed shortly after the events of Monsters of Men, a small expedition is sent out to explore the northern parts of New World. This includes the characters Lee and Wilf, and is found at the end of most new editions of MoM. Lee mentions in it that this is the first 'real' expedition away from the river where the first settlers landed, due to fact that they didn't have resources to spare for an expedition, or really the time/man-power... they were fighting for survival, fighting each other, and fighting the Spackle. It's also important to note that the group of settlers Todd's parents belonged to were religious settlers, and didn't have a lot of advanced technology like Viola's convoy did, even though they left at roughly the same time.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link742473" title="Flag this answer as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=742473&amp;resource_type=CommunityAnswer&amp;return_url=%2Fquestions%2F1347124-the-whole-series-seems-to-be-set-along-the%2Fanswers%2F742473-nobody-leaves-in-the">flag</a>
</div>

<div id="review_86455284" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86455284" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86455284?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310276" href="/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=yes-yes-yes">yes-yes-yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86455284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3631166345150310719">I am shocked. I am speechless. I don't even think I can do this book justice by writing this review. My first reaction is just to scream "OH MY EFFING GOD!!!" (only I don't say "effing"! heh heh … Well, if you've read the books you get the joke) … which is exactly what I said about fifty times after I finished reading it last night.<br/><br/>Seriously, it isn't often that a book like this comes along. I don't think a book has left me feeling this shocked and amazed in years––not even the first two books, </span>
  <span id="freeText3631166345150310719" style="display:none">I am shocked. I am speechless. I don't even think I can do this book justice by writing this review. My first reaction is just to scream "OH MY EFFING GOD!!!" (only I don't say "effing"! heh heh … Well, if you've read the books you get the joke) … which is exactly what I said about fifty times after I finished reading it last night.<br /><br />Seriously, it isn't often that a book like this comes along. I don't think a book has left me feeling this shocked and amazed in years––not even the first two books, which also totally blew my mind.<br /><br />All right, well, let's get down to business. I should stop ranting and get to reviewing.<br /><br />So, Monsters of Men is the third book in Patrick Ness's amazingamazingamazing trilogy, Chaos Walking. As I already said, the first two books––<i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i> and <i>The Ask and the Answer</i>––absolutely blew me away, so I had very high expectations for the final chapter. Of course, when you have high expectations, you get nervous, too. I didn't know how on earth Ness was going to end this or what he was going to do with it … but I trusted him to write something incredible. And ohmygoodness he totally exceeded those very high expectations.<br /><br />Ha, so, funny story about this book. It came out in the UK in early May, and it is not scheduled to come out in the United States until late September. I was just about to explode with impatience, and I totally would have died if I'd had to wait that long. Fortunately someone told me about this website, The Book Depository, which allows you to order books from other countries with free shipping. (YESSSS!!!) So I ordered it and it came for me in the mail yesterday (after my last day of school, too! talk about the best day ever!) and I pretty much read it nonstop from 3:30 to 11:30. I even took it to my sister's middle-school graduation and read it standing up, because I could not bear to put it down. Teehee.<br /><br />So, anyway. The book. I do not even know where to begin. AL;KDFJSJF;SJKFD. Yeah, that's about all I have to say. Just kidding. But really, I'm trying to find the words to write this.<br /><br />Basically, these books are emotionally exhausting. I don't know how else to put it. You become so attached to Todd and Viola and you see them go through so much terrifying crap and it's just like … aaahhh … It gives you that total feeling of dread that eats away at the inside of your stomach, and your eyes are glued to the page and it's like "HOLY CRAP! What if one of them dies or both of them dies or AGGGH??!!! NO NO NO PATRICK NESS WOULDN'T DO THAT … Oh wait, he totally would. CRAP!" I was hardly breathing the whole time I was reading this. And at the end my heart was literally pounding because I was so shocked and so terrified and so devastated and so amazed and I had tears in my eyes and I was about to scream at the book and … GAH. Trust me, it takes a LOT for a book to affect me like this. Okay, I am hyperventilating all over again, just thinking about it. Moving on.<br /><br />So, Todd and Viola. Let's talk about them, because I love them like they were actual people. Firstly Todd … He has been our beloved narrator since book one––he's a sweetheart, he's funny, he's honest, he's confused, he's completely believable … And in Monsters of Men I loved him more than ever. He is definitely one of my favorite main characters of all time. I totally felt for him in this one, and it was heartbreaking to see how he gets caught up in the horrors of war … yet, his dedication to Viola keeps him from completely losing himself. (Awwww &lt;3) And Viola is totally awesome too––strong and determined, and just as dedicated to Todd as he is to her. (AWWWWW! I'm gonna make myself cry. *sniffles*) Their adorable relationship really drives the plot along. Just about everything Todd and Viola do, they do for each other. Although the story is dark, disturbing, and violent, at its heart it is ultimately a story about how love triumphs over war.<br /><br />Patrick Ness. Let's talk about him now, because he actually IS a real person, and in my opinion he is a writing GOD. I know that a lot of people turn away from this series complaining that the writing gives them a headache. (Poopies on them. GRRR. Wait, what? I didn't say that.) And what these people don't recognize is something called originality, which I dare to say most authors lack these days. So, yes, Patrick Ness does write in a stream-of-consciousness style––one-sentence paragraphs, paragraphs that break off in the middle, occasionally spelling words phonetically, switching perspectives every two pages … And yeah, it takes a while to get used to it. I didn't like the first book when I started it, but after about 100 pages or so I got hooked, and I have been addicted to this series ever since. Part of its true power is in Ness's writing. Although it's not the typical "good" writing style, meaning it defies quite a few grammar rules, it is truly amazing writing. There's a difference between being a bad writer and making a <i>choice</i> to not write in a typical style. In this case, it's the latter, and it pays off. Patrick Ness writes in a concise manner––carefully choosing words and images so that each one is meaningful and sticks permanently in the reader's head. His writing is raw, emotional, and completely haunting. And it manages to do this while still being very subtle––that is, Ness doesn't have to outright say things to make them obvious, and that somehow makes them more powerful. I don't know how else to explain it, but you have to read it to see what I mean. I tried to do some writing last night after I finished reading and I just couldn't because I felt like I'd been put to shame! I'm not saying I want to steal his style, but I can only hope that I will find a writing style of my own that will affect someone as powerfully as his has affected and inspired me. :)<br /><br />This book is truly, truly amazing. It's a fascinating exploration of human nature and every aspect of it––how we make war when we want peace, how violence destroys us and how love heals us, how we mature from girls and boys to women and men, how love influences the choices we make … I could go on and on. But over all, these books are astounding, compelling, heartbreaking, touching, terrifying, and haunting. This is by far one of the best books and one of the best series I have ever read in my entire life, and if you have not read them you are missing out on an amazing story. GO READ THEM NOW. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3631166345150310719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_140979711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140979711" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140979711?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406326123" href="/book/show/8100904-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140979711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5643800972948318145">After falling completely in love with the first two books in the Chaos Walking Trilogy, it made perfect sense for me to seek out the final installment asap. And I must admit, my immediate thoughts were mixed. This book doesn't share the fast pace of 'The Knife Of Never Letting Go' and doesn't put as much emphasis on the shock factor like 'The Ask And The Answer'. But it delivered beautifully in a way I could never have imagined.<br/><br/>Firstly, I've never been a fan of rapidly alternating perspectives, </span>
  <span id="freeText5643800972948318145" style="display:none">After falling completely in love with the first two books in the Chaos Walking Trilogy, it made perfect sense for me to seek out the final installment asap. And I must admit, my immediate thoughts were mixed. This book doesn't share the fast pace of 'The Knife Of Never Letting Go' and doesn't put as much emphasis on the shock factor like 'The Ask And The Answer'. But it delivered beautifully in a way I could never have imagined.<br /><br />Firstly, I've never been a fan of rapidly alternating perspectives, but not only does Patrick Ness make it enjoyable, he also makes it necessary. The introduction of the third perspective and it being good old 1017, hell bent on vengeance, is just incredible. I like the careful way Ness makes the lines between heroes and villains very blurred. Is Madame Coyle a freedom-fighter or a terrorist? Are a few innocent lives worth casting aside if what you're trying to achieve benefits the larger numbers? This book is a political statement as well as a great adventure story. A question about the nature of humanity as well as a vivid, entertaining read.<br /><br />Ness constantly delivers surprise after surprise. I don't want to say too much about that and ruin the novel, but the ending was the most shocking one I have read in such a long time... I cried. Literally cried and I just couldn't believe that it happened. <br /><br />This is an astonishing, thought-provoking, important novel. It will stay with me for a very long time.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5643800972948318145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_603429359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452007230p2/8377084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/603429359?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anushka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anushka" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka">Anushka</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406326123" href="/book/show/8100904-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Just read it already!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=sci-fi-dystopia">sci-fi-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=liked-it">liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=them-feels">them-feels</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603429359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7827663896335662783">Also find this review <a href='http://neverstopreadin.blogspot.com/2013/09/chaoswalking3.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>on Don't Stop Readin'</a><br/><br/><b>OH. MY. GOD.<br/><br/>I-<br/>CAN’T-<br/>EVEN-<br/></b><br/><br/>Page <b>572</b><br/>It will<i> always</i> haunt me.<br/>I will <i>never</i> be able to forget it.<br/>It was when I started crying hysterically until my throat started <i>aching</i>.<br/><br/>There are not enough adjectives in the dictionary to sing praises of this series. I am simply tongue-tied by the brilliance of this trilogy, the depth of the topics explored via the characters in this book. <br/>I really cannot write a proper review, I just can’t. I am so severely shocked and utte</span>
  <span id="freeText7827663896335662783" style="display:none">Also find this review <a href="http://neverstopreadin.blogspot.com/2013/09/chaoswalking3.html" rel="nofollow noopener">on Don't Stop Readin'</a><br /><br /><b>OH. MY. GOD.<br /><br />I-<br />CAN’T-<br />EVEN-<br /></b><br /><br />Page <b>572</b><br />It will<i> always</i> haunt me.<br />I will <i>never</i> be able to forget it.<br />It was when I started crying hysterically until my throat started <i>aching</i>.<br /><br />There are not enough adjectives in the dictionary to sing praises of this series. I am simply tongue-tied by the brilliance of this trilogy, the depth of the topics explored via the characters in this book. <br />I really cannot write a proper review, I just can’t. I am so severely shocked and utterly awestruck, it is as if someone has pulled a rug right from under me.<br /><br />I feel like I am a part of an elite club after reading this masterpiece and I feel bad for the people who haven’t read this yet. I genuinely do. This trilogy is not just some sheepish young-adult fantasy thrown together; it is so much different, so much beyond it. Every character is so strong and of significance, that you cannot help but admire Ness's imagination. <br /><br />The predicament, whether we’re on the wrong side or right side in a war is a main theme of this book too. Like I said in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601342753" rel="nofollow noopener"> my review of The Ask and the Answer</a>, Patrick Ness is the one with power here. He can manipulate his readers just like Mayor Prentiss was able to manipulate Todd. <br />When all the ugly faces of war are presented, you cannot decide on whose side you’d want to be because he shows that there is no side with best intentions, you can never completely agree with one person’s idea of winning it.<br /><br />These books should not be categorised as middle-grade/ya books, even adults should read them. It is an excellent, thought-provoking series recommended to all, although I agree with others that 3rd book did not follow the path 2nd and 1st books went on, it still was a moving read and extremely deserving to be the closing chapter of this immensely emotional and powerful ride.<br /><br />On <u>Page 402</u> there is a line -<br /><br /><b>“ And I wait for a long minute.<br />And I don’t know what to say.<br />And I don’t know what to do. "</b><br /><br />That is <b>exactly</b> how I feel right now. <br />Throughout the book there are at least a dozen plot twists but it is the ending that entirely makes you fall in love with <i>Monsters of Men</i>. It is so unbelievable that you will have to read the same line over and over again with teary eyes to fully grasp what's happening.<br /><br /><b> <u>PATRICK NESS.</u><br />I bow to thee.<br /></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7827663896335662783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2348410728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2348410728" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310276" href="/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2348410728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17102414580637123221"><b>THIS FLIPPIN BOOK. I swear I just ran a 45 kilometre race because I'm exhausted.</b> And I'm angry. Ohhhhh you made me SO ANGRY you little black hearted book. It is good though, it is very very good, although I'm still kind of salty at it but giving it 5-stars because you know when you love something a lot but you also want to slap it??? Me @ Chaos Walking.<br/><br/><b>CAN WE TAKE A MOMENT TO SHOUT ABOUT THAT ENDING.</b> I'm traumatised and damaged but very pleased ultimately, because what is the bookworm life if no</span>
  <span id="freeText17102414580637123221" style="display:none"><b>THIS FLIPPIN BOOK. I swear I just ran a 45 kilometre race because I'm exhausted.</b> And I'm angry. Ohhhhh you made me SO ANGRY you little black hearted book. It is good though, it is very very good, although I'm still kind of salty at it but giving it 5-stars because you know when you love something a lot but you also want to slap it??? Me @ Chaos Walking.<br /><br /><b>CAN WE TAKE A MOMENT TO SHOUT ABOUT THAT ENDING.</b> I'm traumatised and damaged but very pleased ultimately, because what is the bookworm life if not emotional damage. #sobsob I actually was sending my friend sob/ragey texts due to the trauma and predicting the most horrible things to happen. Only 87% of my predictions were right. Only 88% of me is on the ground right now. <b><i>But</i>: I do think the book balanced absolute mass murder of feels + with satisfaction. </b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ i think we can all agree PATRICK NESS SHOULD NOT BE ALLOWED ANIMALS. He frikkin had to go and kill Acorn. What did that horse ever do to him??? First Manchee, then Acorn, and both are so loyal and beautiful and DIED TO SAVE DUMB HUMANS. I can't even. <br /><br />Also I kneeeew Todd was going to die. I was so MAD when he died, and then it was only a fake-death so he came back and I'm still an emotional wreck thanks for that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>I was a little disappointed it was basically a 600 page battle though.</b> It DID balance it out with a lot of scenes were other things happened, so not just fighting, but <b>dude, did it drag at times.</b> I got really tired of how often we cycled through everyone's same-same thoughts...too much thinking, not enough action, my friends. So somehow this isn't my most favourite book of the series but it's still getting 5 stars because I'm just proud of myself for surviving the whole thing.<br /><br /><b>PS. The audio is fabulous! 10/10!</b> I listened to all three, and they do effects for the Noise and the narrator is perfection. It makes me super excited for the movie haha.<br /><br /><b>LITTLE THINGS TO NOTE:</b><br />• I absolutely 100% ship 1017 and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ben <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Do not argue with me. They will be married at dawn (so say I anyway).<br />• I cannot even believe how beautiful and innocent and pure Viola/Todd are AND THEY HAVE LIKE 1 KISS IN 3 BOOKS.<br />• And like book 3 they finally hold hands...like woah getting racy here.<br />• It still makes me mad that Viola was salty about trusting Todd without his Noise. I mean, woman, how hypocritical?! When they first met and Todd was basically calling her brain-dead for not having Noise, she was SO MAD. Just because someone doesn't lay out all their secret, doesn't mean they're not trustworthy for goodness sakes.<br />• I LOVED THAT WE GOT THE SPACKLE'S POINT OF VIEW. That added so much!<br />• Lee annoys me and if he could just lie down quietly in a hole somewhere that'd be great.<br />• The Mayor's obsession with Todd was <i>so frikkin creepy</i>.<br />• Everyone is so angry here and hitting everything.<br />• No one ever eats in this whole series and I need to talk to someone about my children's health, this is not ok or fair.<br />• It is 600 pages and I'm sO tiREd<br />• I think the moral of this series is that humans are trash and this is pretty true go us for our excellent relationship skills. Redeemable trash tho. But still. Stahp.<br />• I'm still confused that the audio pronounces Viola as "Vy-la" and I'm here saying "Vi-o-la" like the instrument. WHO'S RIGHT. Obviously must be me.<br />• Was the ending a bit easy??? I'm not sure I'm just so emotionally DRAINED.<br />• Todd being reunited with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ben <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> broke me into such a mess omg.<br />• This has so many layers and emotions and complicated humans and it focuses on so so much more than romance and I'M JUST SUCH A FAN. I wish we had more series like this!!!!!<br /><br /><b>Honestly? I love this series. It's tough and bloody and raw.</b> It's honestly super different to most things I get to read with YA, and I just <i>love</i> the complexity and the discussions. I'm so salty at a lot of the decisions, but IT'S GOOD. It's a good series. I'm a wreck. Just go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17102414580637123221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406379181" href="/book/show/36657882-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2595500135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6236680720359998239">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/11/23/monsters-of-men-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/> <i>“Worst is the one who knows better and does nothing.”</i><br/><br/>🌟 In the previous books, the start would always be “relatively” slow and then the pacing picks up till it becomes faster and better. This time, the author started powerfully, with a fast and great thing, a WAR!! I think this book had the best beginning in this series but unfortunately, it was tamed a little bit in the middle.<br/><br/>🌟 There was a 3rd POV in this book and I </span>
  <span id="freeText6236680720359998239" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/11/23/monsters-of-men-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /> <i>“Worst is the one who knows better and does nothing.”</i><br /><br />🌟 In the previous books, the start would always be “relatively” slow and then the pacing picks up till it becomes faster and better. This time, the author started powerfully, with a fast and great thing, a WAR!! I think this book had the best beginning in this series but unfortunately, it was tamed a little bit in the middle.<br /><br />🌟 There was a 3rd POV in this book and I am not going to spoil it because it was creative and is better to be left a surprise. I am not sure if I was a big fan of the writing style of that character because it took me a while to get used to it and it was confusing at first!<br /><br />🌟 Not to be confused with the general writing style, which is as good as ever!<br /><br /> <i> “Choices may be unbelievably hard but they’re never impossible. To say you have no choice is to release yourself from responsibility and that’s not how a person with integrity acts.” </i><br /><br />🌟 I think the world building and characters are as realistic as ever! These are surely things that I won’t forget quickly. I just didn’t like the continuous Bickering between President Prentiss (one of the smartest “Villains” I have ever read)and Mistress Coyle. It was one of the reason that made the middle part less interesting.<br /><br />🌟 The Plot is great and there are twists and drama and darkness as usual that will destroy you in the best possible way!<br /><br />🌟 Summary: A great continuation of the series that is almost guaranteed not to disappoint you. With a new POV, new twists and new developments that will leave your mouth hanging open! I ended up giving this book and the trilogy as a whole 4 out of 5 stars!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_242575175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242575175" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242575175?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310276" href="/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242575175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10061281984992671380">this lower-than-five-stars rating is probably my fault. i had to put the book down because of life (stupid life) so there was a whole day there where i didn't get to read a single word of this, and i may have simply lost my momentum as a result.<br/><br/>this book is still fantastic. <br/><br/>it is a slower-paced, more meditative book than the other two. before, it was all breakneck excitement and every time the characters seemed to be able to pause for breath - blammo! another effing tragedy! which strangely, did</span>
  <span id="freeText10061281984992671380" style="display:none">this lower-than-five-stars rating is probably my fault. i had to put the book down because of life (stupid life) so there was a whole day there where i didn't get to read a single word of this, and i may have simply lost my momentum as a result.<br><br>this book is still fantastic. <br><br>it is a slower-paced, more meditative book than the other two. before, it was all breakneck excitement and every time the characters seemed to be able to pause for breath - blammo! another effing tragedy! which strangely, did not come across as gratuitous. ness is such a strong writer that he never let the story become "expected" or tedious - there was always a healthy ratio of character-building to adrenaline rushes, so it never seemed that he was just putting explosions and death in the way to make sure you were still paying attention.<br><br>because obviously we are paying attention.<br><br>this one had a more philosophical cast to it than the first two. that is not to say there is no action - there are battles and smaller skirmishes and many innocent characters have terrible things happen to them, so it is very similar in that way to the first two books, with more politics-of-war and musings on the nature and meaning of humanity. everything is cast in shades of gray, where good guys have bad days and bad guys occasionally do the right thing. ness is always about three steps ahead of the reader's expectayshuns (also, much less of <i>that</i> in this final book), and it is nearly impossible to predict what is about to happen.<br><br>however, and i am probably going to get slapped all over the internet about this, i really wasn't into the voice of the return/land/sky. while i understand intellectually that it is necessary to include that perspective and it gives a depth to the story that is important and that the book could not have reached a satisfying conclusion without including it, emotionally, i found it dry and less heart-shredding than viola and todd's story. <br><br>i know.<br><br>but it's true. whenever i came to that font, i was like "nooo - gimmie more viola!!" it's not my fault that those two characters are so close to my heart, while the land is interesting but not all up in my emotional grill.<br><br>this really was an excellent conclusion to one of the finest trilogies i have ever read. both todd and viola grow so much as characters, it is a phenomenal series for that part alone. and the rest - ahhhh. i can't say enough good about this series. <br><br>having just experienced a bug-holocaust and still reeling from toxic fumes, it is probably best to end here, so i can escape to clearer air. effing bugs. i would like to band <i>them</i> and see how they like it...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10061281984992671380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_307483291" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307483291" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4482859-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362722484p2/4482859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307483291?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/4482859-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11201971-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307483291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8600406887074016857">Sometimes you get to the final book in a series, and it feels like a different author is writing it, that the <em>real</em> author who began the story back at book one packed a suitcase and got a one-way ticket to some far-off place. This is how I feel about <em>Monsters of Men</em>, which is really the proverbial nail in the <em>Chaos Walking</em> trilogy's coffin. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men?format=html&rating=5' rel='nofollow noopener'>I've read several glowing reviews for this book</a>, and I admit I struggle to see many of the things those readers are seeing. While everyone's entitled to their</span>
  <span id="freeText8600406887074016857" style="display:none">Sometimes you get to the final book in a series, and it feels like a different author is writing it, that the <em>real</em> author who began the story back at book one packed a suitcase and got a one-way ticket to some far-off place. This is how I feel about <em>Monsters of Men</em>, which is really the proverbial nail in the <em>Chaos Walking</em> trilogy's coffin. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men?format=html&amp;rating=5" rel="nofollow noopener">I've read several glowing reviews for this book</a>, and I admit I struggle to see many of the things those readers are seeing. While everyone's entitled to their own opinions—enjoyment is subjective—I believe readers are less likely to enjoy this trilogy when the books are read consecutively. I can see how waiting a year between books might result in one forgetting the little bits and pieces Ness inserted into his world, and so their absence might not be so frustrating and noticeable. I don't believe I'd <em>like</em> this book with such a wait between readings, but I suspect I wouldn't find the problems as glaring as I do now. When reading the books back to back, the numerous technical flaws with Ness' writing are impossible to ignore.<br><br>By far, Ness' biggest problem in <em>Monsters of Men</em> is technique. It's strange to say that, considering I so love his technique in <em>The Knife of Never Letting Go</em>, but there's a vast difference, and I would say <em>declining quality</em>, between the first and last books of this trilogy. <br><br>Ness continues his sloppy perspective-switching from <em>The Ask and the Answer</em>—and it unfortunately gets worse. Whereas most of the perspective-switching in book two was between chapters, it's between <em>scenes</em> in <em>Monsters of Men</em>. One 400-word scene switches to another 400-word scene from a different perspective, then back again, and on and on. If not for POV headings, readers would struggle to keep up. (Although, the characters spend so much time screaming each other's names that you're never entirely lost. VIOLA! TODD! VIOLA! MARCIA, MARCIA, MARCIA!) Typographical differences are meant to exist between the different points of view, too, but I found this was a little inconsistent for me in the ebook format for Nook. In other words, if you're dying to read this, do so in print.<br><br>There's eventually so much perspective switching that Todd and Viola not only don't sound like themselves from previous books, they halfway morph into some near-schizophrenic first person point of view. Either Todd has an educated, though immature, female alter ego or Viola's got an illiterate, redneck boy living inside her. Neither feels quite right. Worse yet, Ness adds in <em>another</em> first person perspective. It should be said that <strong>not everything needs to be known about everyone at all times in a book</strong>. If a writer thinks otherwise, to any degree, he or she should almost certainly be writing in third person, not first. This is basic stuff, and I'm dismayed Ness had no editor come to his rescue.<br><br>It's difficult for me to look past technical issues to see positives in character development, but I think Ness fails to deliver on this front, too. For Todd and Viola, I can see where he attempts to show development, but it's lost in the perspective chaos (no pun intended) and the ever-conveniently-changing plot device that the Noise becomes. <br><br>Character development is far worse with Mayor Prentiss, <em>Chaos Walking</em>'s bad guy who's meant to disturb readers with his near-unending cruelty and unhinged understanding of the world. I waited and hoped for some deep revelation about Prentiss and his behavior, but he really only becomes an idiotic, <em>grinning</em> sideshow. I should have known not to expect much when the book <em>opened</em> with this dialogue:<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"War," says Mayor Prentiss, his eyes glinting. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S-cbOl96RFM" rel="nofollow noopener">"At last."</a></em>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374319i/728322.gif" alt="Snidely Whiplash" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>Mistress Coyle is a better-written bad guy. She's all about control and power, and readers know enough about her history to know some of the reasons <em>why</em> she behaves the way she does. But Mistress Coyle is not the bad guy readers were introduced to in book one, and though she's of a similar nature to Prentiss, she is the lesser of evils, whether Ness intended for her to be or not. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yeah, she chooses to be a suicide bomber to prove a point, but she didn't try to kill every woman on the planet, now, did she? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>That Mistress Coyle is a mildly interesting and believable bad guy doesn't really matter, though. The <em>whole trilogy</em> falls flat and ultimately makes no sense if we don't understand Mayor Prentiss' history and motives. The previous war with the Spackle, the <em>genocide</em> of women in Prentisstown and his subsequent rise to power there, the connection to Preacher Aaron's religious fundamentalism, the chasing of Todd "for his innocence," the chasing of Viola, his overtaking of all settlements between Prentisstown and Haven, his continued hatred of Spackle and women, his love of war, his interest in Viola's people, his ability to control minds, and countless other things make no sense if readers aren't given details. He doesn't seem to care about fame or fortune—or even power, <em>really</em>—just mind games and war. Without more behind his behavior, he becomes a stock character, mere decoration for Ness' moral and political messages, and a placeholder for true conflict. <br><br>I'm going to "spoil" the big "secret" about Mayor Prentiss for you: He's crazy and bad to the bone. That's it.<br><br>That brings me back to Ness' philosophical messages against war and violence. An inadequate handling of Mayor Prentiss muddles the message Ness is trying to get out to young people. Prentiss is not a realistic portrayal of real-world evil, and so any pacifistic messages surrounding him crumble. Everything's made more awkward when Ness pulls out the old <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/NobleSavage" rel="nofollow noopener">Noble Savage trope</a> for the Spackle. They are glorified Native Americans, right down to their peace-seeking chieftain and his elaborate headpiece. Todd and Viola's response to the world they live in can't deliver important life lessons because their world no longer mirrors any sort of reality by the end of this book. All the good and evil has been created using cookie-cutter stereotypes. <br><br>Other young adult authors have better communicated how difficult it is to understand and cope with the hows and whys of people's behavior, as well as how unclear appropriate courses of action can be. While Ness accomplishes some of the latter in <em>Monsters of Men</em> through Todd and Viola, he struggles to portray the former because of his poor development of Mayor Prentiss. If only the evil men of our world were more like Ness portrays Prentiss: void of political, moral, and financial motivations and connections. It wouldn't be so difficult to know how to respond to them. <br><br>These are just some of the problems with this book. Questions are left unanswered, too many characters prove to be unimportant, and the ending can only be described as an anticlimactic showdown reminiscent of every bad superhero movie ever made. <br><br>I still think <em>The Knife of Never Letting Go</em> is a fun read, which is why I can't bring myself to give this book the one-star rating it may very well deserve, but <em>The Ask and the Answer</em> and <em>Monsters of Men</em> are disappointing followups. This trilogy had potential, but Ness ultimately doesn't deliver.<br><br><a href="http://fantastikate.com/reading/" title="Visit Fantastikate.com for more book reviews." rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340956i/697219.png" alt="Fantastikate Logo" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>========================================<br><strong>Quotes From the Book</strong><br><em>(Apply your own positive/negative connotations.) </em><br>========================================<br><br>That’s the nasty, nasty secret of war- When yer winning- When yer winning, it’s ruddy thrilling—<br><br>---<br><br>And then I turn to the Mayor and I’m filled with her, with her love for me and my love for her- And it makes me big as an effing mountain-</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8600406887074016857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2369145867" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369145867?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406326123" href="/book/show/8100904-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=500-page-plus">500-page-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=end-of-the-world">end-of-the-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369145867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10434008346127113560">3.5 stars ⭐️ <br/><br/>I liked this, it was enjoyable. I just didn’t seem to find it as mind blowing and life altering as some other readers. <br/><br/><i> “War makes monsters of men.” </i><br/><br/>I was never bored, but I feel this novel could have been cut down by a few hundred pages. A good 300 pages in was just back and forth war between the people of New Prentisstown, Mistress Coyle’s group and the Spackle. <br/><br/>But there was plenty I did like <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I loved Ben’s return,  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that he had become like a mes</span>
  <span id="freeText10434008346127113560" style="display:none">3.5 stars ⭐️ <br /><br />I liked this, it was enjoyable. I just didn’t seem to find it as mind blowing and life altering as some other readers. <br /><br /><i> “War makes monsters of men.” </i><br /><br />I was never bored, but I feel this novel could have been cut down by a few hundred pages. A good 300 pages in was just back and forth war between the people of New Prentisstown, Mistress Coyle’s group and the Spackle. <br /><br />But there was plenty I did like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I loved Ben’s return,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that he had become like a messenger between the men and the Spackle. I liked the small sci fi elements, including the spaceship and the technology that came with it. <br /><br />Overall, I loved Todd and Viola’s relationship. The strength they drew from one another even when the other had made terrible mistakes. Also the ending was satisfying <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the Mayor finally admitting he had lost his mind after hearing the entire worlds noise most of his life, he felt he needed to destroy the world to make it quiet again. Also Todd’s ‘death’ I’m glad it left us with hope that he is coming back.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Entertaining, with good characters and villains, an interesting New World to experience. </span>

<div id="review_302984652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302984652" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302984652?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310276" href="/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog">blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302984652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2218216746931562335">If you read my reviews of <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i> and <i>The Ask and the Answer</i>, you'll find that I was a smitten kitten with the <i>Chaos Walking</i> series. In the carbon copy world of young adult literature, these are inventive books with powerful themes resonating throughout. I have been anticipating the moment when I would finish the last book in the trilogy, expecting to savor the return to Todd and Viola's world. So what effin' happened that led to a tepid 3 star rating? I'm still trying to f</span>
  <span id="freeText2218216746931562335" style="display:none">If you read my reviews of <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i> and <i>The Ask and the Answer</i>, you'll find that I was a smitten kitten with the <i>Chaos Walking</i> series. In the carbon copy world of young adult literature, these are inventive books with powerful themes resonating throughout. I have been anticipating the moment when I would finish the last book in the trilogy, expecting to savor the return to Todd and Viola's world. So what effin' happened that led to a tepid 3 star rating? I'm still trying to figure it out.<br /><br />Maybe it was series fatigue or maybe I waited too long between reading books 2 and 3 (I hate getting locked into series books, so that is a possibility). For whatever reason, <i>Monsters of Men</i> never grabbed me in the way the first two books did. It felt repetitive. War with the Spackle, conflict between Mayor Prentiss and Mistress Coyle, Todd and Viola don't know what to do, and round and round it goes. Each time I picked up the book, I felt like it was <i>Groundhog Day</i>--I could have sworn I read the same damn thing yesterday. The war is somewhat anticlimactic and I never felt any real tension. I'm rather out of sorts about this because I feel as though I somehow let down the book instead of the book letting me down. Did I miss something? Is there something I'm just not getting? These are the thoughts that plague me because I wanted, nay, needed to love this book. And I just didn't. Todd and Viola's angst over being separated is irritating to me because I could not for the life of me understand why they insisted on being apart ("Just walk your ass up the damn hill, Todd," I kept encouraging him throughout, but he never listened), Mayor Prentiss doesn't seem like that big of a bad ass threat, and the one twist the novel is relying on is fairly predictable.<br /><br />Despite this, I liked the addition of the narration from 1017's point of view. Told in the language of the indigenous people of New World, Ness does a good job of making the voice seem alien and foreign. These chapters are somewhat difficult to read in terms of adjusting to the syntax and invented phrases, but it added to my ability to believe in the Spackle as a separate sentient species from humans. Also, the questions raised (is there morality in war, what makes a terrorist, how do we know when we can trust our leaders, is violence ever justified) are all complex and worthy of our attention. Ness skillfully asks these questions without glorifying war nor necessarily vilifying it, which makes this an above average young adult read.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Insignificant Cinder</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2218216746931562335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126603182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126603182" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126603182?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781406310276" href="/book/show/7540092-monsters-of-men">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Yes, Aaron... E.V.E.R.Y.O.N.E!!!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126603182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8918375140009361072">Two words: <b>Emotional Investment.</b> <br/><br/>This review is me on a soapbox <s>telling</s> shouting at anyone/everyone within hearing distance to <b>read it… NOW!</b> So, I guess, this review isn't a review after all. Right before I started Monsters, I was so worried if Ness would kill off one, some, or all his characters. Then I asked myself, “Is that all you can think of?” My response: a resounding, YES! My concern extending to the living or dying of these people, clearly establishes my emotional investment. If someone</span>
  <span id="freeText8918375140009361072" style="display:none">Two words: <b>Emotional Investment.</b> <br /><br />This review is me on a soapbox <s>telling</s> shouting at anyone/everyone within hearing distance to <b>read it… NOW!</b> So, I guess, this review isn't a review after all. Right before I started Monsters, I was so worried if Ness would kill off one, some, or all his characters. Then I asked myself, “Is that all you can think of?” My response: a resounding, YES! My concern extending to the living or dying of these people, clearly establishes my emotional investment. If someone were to complain about the eye dialect or what not, I’d probably <s>rabidly</s> say… “But that’s the point! Prentiss destroyed any chance they had of getting educated. He had the schools burned… They can’t help being the way they are!” If someone were to point out that its monstrous size just covers a lot of violence, I’d (again) say, “Because that’s the way it is… Sans rainbows and robins, the world can be violent and ugly… but at least there’s some hope.” So, yes I’m probably too close to the characters; too much a loyal fan of the series to say anything unbiased about the books and the people in it. <br /><br />I will say that Monsters of Men is <b>not</b> an easy read, at all. It’s…<br /><br /><b>INTENSE. <br /><br />ORIGINAL. <br /><br />GUT-WRENCHING.</b> <br /><br />Why? There are so many themes in it~ love, violence, prejudice… heck, it could be about hope (or its absence.) But there’s a distinct absence of a self-righteous voice. All of them admit to doing horrendous things; none claim perfection or total goodness. I <b>love</b> that absence. That typical dichotomy of us = good and them = bad is absent. Basically, it says to me that we are all capable of being monsters. Or more aptly, there are only people~ all capable of doing bad things; all capable of doing good things. That it’s all a matter of choice.<br /><br />So, yeah, this is me, still on my soapbox… still insisting that people get there hands on this series. Love it, hate it... <b>just read it!</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8918375140009361072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
